        <meta property="og:url" content="https://pubs.acs.org/doi/full/10.1021/acsami.7b14673"><meta property="og:title" content="Amorphous P2S5/C Composite as High-Performance Anode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries"><meta property="og:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b14673/asset/images/acsami.7b14673.social.jpeg_v03"><meta property="og:description" content="We show a general method for achieving high-performance sodium storage materials via transforming crystalline P2S5 to amorphous P2S5 adhered to carbon matrix. The amorphous P2S5/C composite shows unique structural characteristics differing from the crystalline, which is identified by X-ray diffraction (XRD), Raman spectroscopy, transmission electron microscope (TEM) and so on. The amorphous P2S5/C composite exhibits a safe average potential of 0.82 V, a reversible capacity of 400 mA h g–1, a remarkable capacity retention of 89.4% over 4000 cycles as well as good rate capability. Our findings open up opportunities to design of advanced anodes for room-temperature sodium-ion batteries."><meta property="og:type" content="Article"><meta property="og:site_name" content="ACS Publications"><meta name="twitter:card" content="summary_large_image"><meta name="twitter:site" content="@ACSPublications"><meta name="twitter:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b14673/asset/images/acsami.7b14673.social.jpeg_v03">

<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/wro/1122814~thiss-ds.js" async="" nonce="931887992ef554b8-SJC"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="931887992ef554b8-SJC">

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            timeout: 5000,

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
            },
            retrieveEntity: function (ms) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                if (ms == undefined || ms === '') {
                    ms = this.timeout;
                }

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res.data);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('failed to retrieve entity from local storage: ' + err);
                        });
                    // Set up the timeout
                    setTimeout(function () {
                        reject('Promise timed out ' + ms + ' ms');
                    }, ms);
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage due to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {
                            doi: doi,
                            entityid: entityId,
                            entityTitle: entityTitle,
                            eventGroupKey: '9a0e6de2-8927-4927-9519-3743c97ef22d'
                        }

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    }).fail(function (status) {
                        return reject(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (i = 0; i < allSsoInstitutions.length; i++) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        if(allSsoInstitutions.length === 0 && true){
                            self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, null, null)
                                .then(function () {
                                    console.log('No Entity found');
                                }, function (err) {
                                    console.log('failed to get the none entity status' ,err);
                                });
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            }).catch(function (err) {
                                reject(err);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();

                    if ($('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').length > 0) {
                        let institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox = $('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').get(0);
                        if (!$(institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox).is(":checked")) {
                            return;
                        }
                    }

                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="931887992ef554b8-SJC">
var dfpReady = false;
$(document).ready(function() {
    // var journalTitle = 'applied_materials_interfaces';
    var taxonomyKeywords = $('.article_header-taxonomy');
    var articleKeyword = $('meta[name="keywords"]');
    var articleTitle = $('meta[name="dc.Title"]');
    var articleDescription = $('meta[name="dc.Description"]');
    var abstractKeyword = $('p.articleBody_abstractText:contains("Keywords: ")');
    var searchTerms = [];

    if (taxonomyKeywords.length > 0) {
        $(taxonomyKeywords).children(".rlist--inline").children("li").each(function() {
            searchTerms.push($(this).text());
        });
    }
    else if (articleKeyword.length > 0) { 
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleKeyword.prop('content').split(', '));
    }
    else if (abstractKeyword.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(abstractKeyword.text().split("Keywords: ")[1].split('; '));
    }
    else if (articleDescription.length > 0) {
        $(articleDescription).each(function() {
            articleDescriptionKeywords = $(this).prop('content');
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/.,/g,"");
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/\s{2,}/g," ");
            searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleDescriptionKeywords.split(' '));
        });
    }

    if (articleTitle.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleTitle.prop('content').split(' '));
    }

    googletag.cmd.push(function() {
        var mappingLeader = googletag.sizeMapping().
        addSize([750, 200], [728, 90]). 
        addSize([0, 0], [320, 50]).
        build();
        //leaderboard
        googletag.defineSlot('/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article', [728, 90], 'dfp-journal-article-leaderboard').defineSizeMapping(mappingLeader).setTargeting('location', 'leaderboard1').setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //recommend
        googletag.defineSlot("/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article", [1, 1], "dfp-journal-article-recommend").setTargeting("ntvPlacement", ["1100167"]).setTargeting("location", "recommend").setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //googletag.pubads().enableSingleRequest();
        googletag.pubads().collapseEmptyDivs();
        googletag.pubads().setTargeting('inst',dartInstitutionType).setTargeting('memb',dartMember);
        googletag.pubads().addEventListener("slotRenderEnded", function(event) {
            console.log(event.slot.getSlotElementId() + " isEmpty: " + event.isEmpty + " | creative id: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            if((event.isEmpty === false) && (event.slot.getSlotElementId() != "dfp-journal-article-recommend")) {
                $("#" + event.slot.getSlotElementId()).parents(".advertisement").slideDown();
                console.log("ad display: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            }
            // else {
            //     console.log("no ad found");
            // }
        });
        googletag.enableServices();
        dfpReady = true;
    });
});
</script>

class="article--latest"><div class="figure-viewer"><div class="figure-viewer_row"><div class="figure-viewer_col loop-trap"><div aria-live="polite" aria-atomic="true" class="figure-viewer_modal"><a <script nonce="931887992ef554b8-SJC">
$(function() {
    var serialCode = "aamick";
    var books = ["reagents", "symposium", "advances", "medichemreviews", "styleguide"]
    if(books.includes(serialCode) === false) {
        // default click action
        $("[data-id]").on("mousedown", function(e) {
            var currentClickID = $(this).attr("data-id");

            if(currentClickID.includes("_hover") === false) {
                if(currentClickID.match("^article_") && !currentClickID.match("^article_abstract_CC")) {   
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Amorphous P&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;S&lt;sub&gt;5&lt;/sub&gt;/C Composite as High-Performance Anode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.7b14673", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                }
            }
        });
        
        // Access Management icons hover
        var articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        var articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent === false) {
                articleAccessManagementIconHover = true;
                var articleAccessManagementHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleAccessManagementIconHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Amorphous P&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;S&lt;sub&gt;5&lt;/sub&gt;/C Composite as High-Performance Anode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.7b14673", "Article_Element": articleAccessManagementHover });
    
                        articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        });
    
        // articleRightsPermissionsLink hover
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent === false) {
                articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = true;
                var articleRightsHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Amorphous P&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;S&lt;sub&gt;5&lt;/sub&gt;/C Composite as High-Performance Anode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.7b14673", "Article_Element": articleRightsHover });
    
                        articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        });
    
        // Author hover
        var articleAuthorHover = false
        var articleAuthorHoverEvent = false
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if((articleAuthorHoverEvent === false) && ($(this).parent().hasClass("view-affs") === false)) {
                articleAuthorHover = true;
                var authorInfoHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAuthorHover === true) && (articleAuthorHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Amorphous P&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;S&lt;sub&gt;5&lt;/sub&gt;/C Composite as High-Performance Anode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.7b14673", "Article_Element": authorInfoHover });
    
                        articleAuthorHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAuthorHover = false;
        });
    
        // CC License hover
        var articleAbstractCCHover = false
        var articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = false
        var articleDrawerCCHover = false
        var articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = false
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if($(this).attr("data-id")) {
                if(($(this).attr("data-id") === "article_drawer_CC-License") && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleDrawerCCHover = true;
                    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleDrawerCCHover === true) && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Amorphous P&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;S&lt;sub&gt;5&lt;/sub&gt;/C Composite as High-Performance Anode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.7b14673", "Article_Element": "article_drawer_CC-License_hover" });
    
                            articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
                else if(($(this).attr("data-id").match("^article_abstract_CC")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleAbstractCCHover = true;
    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Amorphous P&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;S&lt;sub&gt;5&lt;/sub&gt;/C Composite as High-Performance Anode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.7b14673", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                            articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
            }
            else if(($(this).hasClass("article__cc-license__link")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = true;
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Amorphous P&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;S&lt;sub&gt;5&lt;/sub&gt;/C Composite as High-Performance Anode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.7b14673", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                        articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            if(articleAbstractCCHover === true) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = false;
            }
            if(articleDrawerCCHover = true) {
                articleDrawerCCHover = false;
            }
        });
        
        // show recommeneded click delay
        var intervalCount = 0;
        var showRecommendedInterval = setInterval(function() {
            intervalCount += 100;
            if($(".show-recommended__wrapper .show-recommended").length > 0) {
                clearInterval(showRecommendedInterval);
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowMore']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Amorphous P&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;S&lt;sub&gt;5&lt;/sub&gt;/C Composite as High-Performance Anode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.7b14673", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowLess']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Amorphous P&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;S&lt;sub&gt;5&lt;/sub&gt;/C Composite as High-Performance Anode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.7b14673", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
            }
        }, 100);
    }
});
</script>

class="articleMetrics_count"><h2>Citations</h2><div class="articleMetrics-val"><a href="#citeThis" class="internalNav">25</a></div></div></div></div><div class="articleMetrics_about"><div class="base data-db-target-of="aboutArticleMetrics" id="about-article-metrics" class="dropBlock__holder"><button class="articleMetrics_close"> <i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-close_thin"></i><span class="sr-only">close</span></button><p>Article Views are the COUNTER-compliant sum of full text article downloads since November 2008 (both PDF and HTML) across all institutions and individuals. These metrics are regularly updated to reflect usage leading up to the last few days.</p><p>Citations are the number of other articles citing this article, calculated by Crossref and updated daily.<a href="https://www.crossref.org/services/cited-by/"> Find more information about Crossref citation counts.</a></p><p>The Altmetric Attention Score is a quantitative measure of the attention that a research article has received online. Find more information on<a href="https://help.altmetric.com/support/solutions/articles/6000233311-how-is-the-altmetric-attention-score-calculated"> the Altmetric Attention Score and how the score is calculated.</a></p></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="article_abstract"><div class="article_abstract-title" id="Abstract" tabindex="0"><h2>Abstract</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div><div class="article_abstract-content hlFld-Abstract" id="abstractBox" property="description"><figure id="f_tgr1" data-index="0" class="article__inlineFigure article_abstract-img"><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img class="inline-fig internalNav" src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b14673/asset/images/medium/am-2017-14673m_0004.gif" alt="" id="tgr1" property="image" style="width:405px; height:275px"></button><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b14673/asset/images/large/am-2017-14673m_0004.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.7b14673&amp;id=f_tgr1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p class="articleBody_abstractText">We show a general method for achieving high-performance sodium storage materials via transforming crystalline P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub> to amorphous P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub> adhered to carbon matrix. The amorphous P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>/C composite shows unique structural characteristics differing from the crystalline, which is identified by X-ray diffraction (XRD), Raman spectroscopy, transmission electron microscope (TEM) and so on. The amorphous P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>/C composite exhibits a safe average potential of 0.82 V, a reversible capacity of 400 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>, a remarkable capacity retention of 89.4% over 4000 cycles as well as good rate capability. Our findings open up opportunities to design of advanced anodes for room-temperature sodium-ion batteries.</p></div><div class="article__cc-license"><div class="article__cc-license__body"><p class="article__cc-license__para">This publication is licensed under the terms of your
                            institutional subscription.

data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_high-performance">high-performance</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="article_content"><div class="article_content-table hlFld-FullText"><div class="article_content-row"><div class="article_content-left" property="articleBody" style="width: 384px;"><p class="first">Lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) have been extensively used in our lives. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref1" aria-label="reference 1">(1)</a> However, the limitation of lithium resources and high cost of lithium cannot match our increasing requirement. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref2" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref2" aria-label="reference 2">(2)</a> With the extensive and low-cost sodium sources, and similar chemistry to lithium, sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have received widespread attention. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref3" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref3" aria-label="reference 3">(3)</a> It is more difficult comparing with LIBs when hunting for a suitable electrode material for SIBs because of the larger and heavier Na<sup>+</sup> than Li<sup>+</sup>. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref4" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref4" aria-label="reference 4">(4)</a> It is known that the formation of dendrite and instability in fast charging–discharging make the metallic sodium not suitable for the anode. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref5" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref5" aria-label="reference 5">(5)</a> P2-type Na<sub>2/3</sub>Co<sub>1/3</sub>Ti<sub>2/3</sub>O<sub>2</sub> <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref6" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref6" aria-label="reference 6">(6)</a> with outstanding cycle stability (84.8% capacity retention for 3000 cycles) and Na<sub>0.66</sub>Ni<sub>0.17</sub>Co<sub>0.17</sub>Ti<sub>0.66</sub>O<sub>2</sub> <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref7" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref7" aria-label="reference 7">(7)</a> serving as both anode and cathode have also been reported. Molybdenum-based oxides like Na<sub>0.3</sub>MoO<sub>2</sub> <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref8" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref8" aria-label="reference 8">(8)</a> is proved a promising anode material for SIBs. Many materials such as Sn, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref9 ref10" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref9 ref10" aria-label="reference 9 and 10">(9, 10)</a> Sb, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref11" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref11" aria-label="reference 11">(11)</a> Ge, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref12" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref12" aria-label="reference 12">(12)</a> P. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref13" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref13" aria-label="reference 13">(13)</a> and binary/ternary composites <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref14 ref15 ref16 ref17 ref18" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref14 ref15 ref16 ref17 ref18" aria-label="reference 14 to 18">(14-18)</a> have also been developed as SIBs anode by conversion and/or alloying/dealloying processes. Herein, we demonstrate a low-cost P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>/C composite anode for SIBs, exhibiting a high capacity of ∼400 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>, a safe average potential of ∼0.82 V, and ultrastable cycling performance without detectable capacity decay. It is acknowledged that crystalline graphite is widely used in LIBs but electrochemically inactive in SIBs. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref19" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref19" aria-label="reference 19">(19)</a> When nongraphitic hard carbon with disordered structure is employed as sodium storage materials, a large capacity is delivered despite that most of capacity of 300 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> corresponds to sodium plating, associated with the safety concern. Herein, we present an amorphization method in P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>/C composite for high-safety and stable-cycling sodium storage materials, which can be applied to other negative materials. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref20" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref20" aria-label="reference 20">(20)</a></p><p>The structure of P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub> (more accurate: P<sub>4</sub>S<sub>10</sub>) is built from P<sub>4</sub> in tetrahedral form, all six sides made of P–P bonds broke by the addition of one sulfur atom between each P atom (turned to P–S–P bonds). <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref21" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref21" aria-label="reference 21">(21)</a> The ball-milling time shows a great influence on the X-ray diffraction (XRD) patterns of crystalline and amorphous P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>, as shown in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig1" aria-label="Figure 1">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>a. XRD reflection of the commercial P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub> (without mixed acetylene black (AB) and ball-milling) exhibits a well-crystallized phase (black line) symbolized by the sharp peaks at around 2θ = 30 and 53°. When the time increases to 70 h, the feature peaks of P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub> completely disappear and only one broad peak at 2θ = 26° exists (blue line) which belongs to AB, suggesting a transformation of crystalline P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub> to amorphous P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub> in the composite. We also synthesized P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>/C composite with 2 and 40 h (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b14673/suppl_file/am7b14673_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S1</a>) ball-milling process to contrast. As shown in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig1" aria-label="Figure 1">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>a, the feature peaks of P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub> still appear (pink line) after short ball-milling (with AB), merely with the reduced intensity and broadening.</p><figure id="fig1" data-index="1" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 1</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b14673/asset/images/medium/am-2017-14673m_0001.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b14673/asset/images/large/am-2017-14673m_0001.jpeg" id="gr1" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 1. (a) XRD patterns of commercial P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub> (black line) and P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>/C composite after 2 h (pink line) and 70 h (blue line) ball-milling; (b) Raman spectra of commercial P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub> and P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>/C composite after 70 h ball-milling; XPS spectra of (c) P 2p and (d) S 2p for the P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>/C composite after 70 h ball-milling.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b14673/asset/images/large/am-2017-14673m_0001.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.7b14673&amp;id=fig1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p>Raman spectra also show a difference between commercial P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub> and P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>/C composite after long-time ball-milling (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig1" aria-label="Figure 1">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>b). Raman spectrum of the commercial P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub> shows the specific stretching vibrations of the P–S–P bond signal at ∼390 cm<sup>–1</sup> and P═S bond at around 686 and 712 cm<sup>–1</sup> (red line), which are the typical Raman fingerprints of P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>, corresponding to the T<sub>2</sub> and A<sub>1</sub> modes. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref22" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref22" aria-label="reference 22">(22)</a> The fingerprints bonds of P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub> also appear after long-time ball-milling, accompanied by the weakening of the intensity and the shift to higher wavenumber (see blue line in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig1" aria-label="Figure 1">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>b, clearer in zoom in figure). The obvious carbon peaks are observed at around 1320 and 1580 cm<sup>–1</sup> for D-band and G-band (blue line), respectively.</p><p>To probe the surface chemical state of the P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>/C composite, X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) was employed. The structure of P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub> is isostructural with that of P<sub>2</sub>O<sub>5</sub>. It is easy to know that there are one species of P and two species of S according to the molecular structure. As shown in the P 2p XPS spectra (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig1" aria-label="Figure 1">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>c), the spectrum has been fitted to the 2p<sup>1/2</sup> and 2p<sup>3/2</sup> doublet, corresponding to a binding energy value 134.6 eV and a splitting value 0.9 eV. Similarly, there are two sulfur species with the binding energy values of 165.3 and 164.2 eV, respectively. Thermogravimetry (TG) and differential thermoanalysis (DTA) were further employed to reveal the proportion of P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub> in P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>/C composite. <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b14673/suppl_file/am7b14673_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S2</a> shows the TG-DTA curves of the commercial P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub> and P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>/C composite after long-time ball-milling. From the curve (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b14673/suppl_file/am7b14673_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S2b</a>) of commercial P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>, it can be found that there is one typical endotherm peak at approximately 270 °C, which is attributed to the melting process of P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>. And there are two main peaks of DTA in the curve of P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>/C composite (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b14673/suppl_file/am7b14673_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S2a</a>), which represent the melting process and oxidation process (720 °C), respectively. The proportion of P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub> in P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>/C composite is about 66.7% which can be easily estimated from the comparison of two figures, and this value is consistent with the initial mass ratio of P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>/AB.</p><p>Scanning electron microscope (SEM) images of commercial P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub> (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b14673/suppl_file/am7b14673_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S3</a>) and P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>/C composite (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig2" aria-label="Figure 2">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>a) after 70 h ball-milling show agglomerated particles with nanoparticles. EDX (energy-dispersive X-ray spectroscopy)-mapping (the area selected in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b14673/suppl_file/am7b14673_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S4</a>) indicates the homogeneous distribution of C, P, and S in the P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>/C composite (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig2" aria-label="Figure 2">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>d–f). No typical Scherrer rings of P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub> are observed after long-time ball-milling (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig2" aria-label="Figure 2">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>c), demonstrating that the crystalline P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub> particles change to an amorphous-like phase. And the amorphous P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub> particles with nanosize are uniformly encapsulated within the carbon matrix. The results are consistent with that of XRD, which have been discussed before.</p><figure id="fig2" data-index="2" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 2</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b14673/asset/images/medium/am-2017-14673m_0002.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b14673/asset/images/large/am-2017-14673m_0002.jpeg" id="gr2" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 2. Images of the amorphous P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>/C composite after 70 h ball-milling. (a) SEM image, (b) TEM image, (c) selected area electron-diffraction pattern, and (d) EDX mapping of carbon, (e) phosphorus, and (f) sulfur.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b14673/asset/images/large/am-2017-14673m_0002.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.7b14673&amp;id=fig2"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p>The initial discharge specific capacity at 100 mA g<sup>–1</sup> with 70 h ball-milling is near 1000 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>, and the charge specific capacity changes to 400 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b14673/suppl_file/am7b14673_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S5a</a>). The d<i>Q</i>/d<i>V</i> curve of the first cycle is shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b14673/suppl_file/am7b14673_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S5b</a>. In the first discharge, several peaks appeared between 0.01 and 1.3 V, including one broad peak, belonging to the formation of solid electrolyte interface (SEI). There is also one small peak located at 0.03 V, which represents the insertion of sodium into AB. In contrast, the initial charge/discharge profiles of P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>@C electrodes were also tested (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b14673/suppl_file/am7b14673_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S6</a>, the ball-milling time between 0 and 70 h). It is obvious that there is almost no plateau for the commercial P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>. The first discharge capacity of pure P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub> is about 60 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> and the stable reversible capacity is merely 14 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>. The profile of the electrode with ball-milling 40 h is similar to the electrode with ball-milling time 70 h, indicating the similar reaction mechanism. The performance of the electrode is the best when it was treated with the longer ball-milling time of 70 h.</p><p>The cycle curves of P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>/C composite after 70 h ball-milling are shown in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig3" aria-label="Figure 3">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>a. A reversible capacity of 396 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> is obtained at 100 mA g<sup>–1</sup> after the initial cycle (based on the mass of P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>). A pattern of overlapping is remarkably found among all the cycles. Moreover, the electrode shows excellent capacity retention upon cycling. Even after 100 cycles, a specific capacity of 394 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> with almost negligible capacity decay is still acquirable. <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig3" aria-label="Figure 3">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>b shows the d<i>Q</i>/d<i>V</i> curves from <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig3" aria-label="Figure 3">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>a. The well overlapping profiles can be found during cycling, indicating its high reversibility. The cycling performance and Coulombic efficiency of P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>/C composite/Na battery can be seen in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig3" aria-label="Figure 3">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>c. The P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>/C composite has a high Coulombic efficiency ranging from 98.6% to 99.7% and the capacity has almost no attenuation. Moreover, a capacity of 308 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> was obtained with the current density of 200 mA g<sup>–1</sup>. And even at higher rates of 400, 1000, and 2000 mA g<sup>–1</sup>, the capacity of 236, 155, and 108 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> were accessible respectively (see <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig3" aria-label="Figure 3">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>d, all capacities base on P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub> after subtracting contribution from AB). Further, the capacity contribution from AB after 70h ball-milling was also evaluated (AB as the anode of the sodium battery) under identical test conditions as shown in  AB). Further, the capacity contribution from AB after 70h ball-milling was also evaluated (AB as the anode of the sodium battery) under identical test conditions as shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b14673/suppl_file/am7b14673_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S7a</a>. It is obvious that the capacity contribution of AB is negligible (about 15 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> after the first cycle). There also exists one broad d<i>Q</i>/d<i>V</i> peak of AB near 0.37 V for the first cycle, which belongs to the decomposition of electrolyte  (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b14673/suppl_file/am7b14673_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S7b</a>). One sharp peak near 0.03 V represents the insertion process of sodium into AB similar to <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b14673/suppl_file/am7b14673_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S5b</a>. Moreover, we also tested a long-time cycling performance with the current density of 2 A g<sup>–1</sup> (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig3" aria-label="Figure 3">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>e). The capacity is stable without any notable decay and the battery could retain 89.4% of the capacity even after more than 4000 cycles, indicating a superior reversible performance.</p><figure id="fig3" data-index="3" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 3</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b14673/asset/images/medium/am-2017-14673m_0003.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b14673/asset/images/large/am-2017-14673m_0003.jpeg" id="gr3" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 3. Electrochemical performance of P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>/C composite after 70 h ball-milling. (a) Typical potential profiles and (b) d<i>Q</i>/d<i>V</i> curves of the second, fifth and 100th cycle; (c) cyclic performance and Coulombic efficiency with 100 mA g<sup>–1</sup>; (d) rate capacity of P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>/C composite; (e) cyclic performance and Coulombic efficiency with 2000 mA g <sup>–1</sup>.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b14673/asset/images/large/am-2017-14673m_0003.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.7b14673&amp;id=fig3"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p>To research the kinetic differences of the P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>/C composites with different ball-milling time, we performed electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) measurements (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b14673/suppl_file/am7b14673_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S8</a>). The curves show the EIS of the electrodes after the initial cycle, respectively. The ball-milling time are 2, 40, and 70 h. The semicircle diameter for P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>/C composite with ball-milling time 70 h is much smaller than that for P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>/C composite with ball-milling time 2h and 40h, indicating the great improvement of electron conductivity (formation of the amorphous structure). The long-time ball-milling is great helpful to promote the electrode kinetics, accounting for a high-rate performance of the P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>/C composite electrode.</p><p>The initial cycle was explored by ex-situ XRD for investigating the reaction mechanism of amorphous P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub> with Na, as shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b14673/suppl_file/am7b14673_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S9</a>. At the beginning of the reaction, there are almost no peaks appear before discharge to 1.0 V (C1). Upon sodiation to 0.3 V (C2), the electrode shows clear peaks which are assigned to NaP, Na<sub>2</sub>S and S. When sodiated to 0 V (C3), the NaP signals vanish and the Na<sub>3</sub>P signals are observed. Note that there is a broad amorphous peak at ∼23° still exists, which is assigned to S, indicating its partial activity. At reversed desodiation process, the peaks returned to their initial state, expect for an irreversible broad peak assigned to S and/or Na<sub>2</sub>S, indicating an irreversible process during cycling. The partial activity of anode, irreversible process, and formation of SEI mainly account for the irreversible capacity of the initial cycle. It is likely that the reaction mechanism may base on the conversion and alloying processes as follows:<span class="NLM_disp-formula" id="ueq1"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b14673/asset/images/am-2017-14673m_m001.gif" alt=""></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula" id="ueq2"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b14673/asset/images/am-2017-14673m_m002.gif" alt=""></span>Literature data of some different anodes on the electrochemical performance is exhibited in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#tbl1" aria-label="Table 1">Table </a><a class="ref showTableEvent internalNav" data-id="tbl1" href="#tbl1">1</a>. It is obvious that P-based anodes show high capacities including the amorphous P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>/C composite. However, the capacity has been found to decline dramatically from 1322 to 186 only after 50 cycles at 100 mA g<sup>–1</sup> (ref  <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref28" aria-label="reference 28">28</a>), corresponding a capacity retention of merely 14.1% which far lower than 89.4% in our result. There are three obvious advantages of the amorphous P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>/C composite compared with other anodes in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#tbl1" aria-label="Table 1">Table </a><a class="ref showTableEvent internalNav" data-id="tbl1" href="#tbl1">1</a>. The first is the capacity: the P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>/C composite shows ∼400 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> during discharge process which is larger than most of the other anodes. The second is capacity retention: the P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>/C composite shows the best capacity retention of 99.5% after 100 cycles at 100 mA g<sup>–1</sup>, followed by 93.0% in hard carbon spherules at 30 mA g<sup>–1</sup>. The third is long-time cycling performance: the P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>/C composite shows an excellent performance with neglectable capacity fading. Other materials show relatively poor performance, which are unsatisfactory for the commercial use. Different from these materials, our results indicate that the amorphous P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>/C composite is capable of sustaining excellent electrochemical performance which may result from the suppression of volume expansion and the interactions between P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub> and AB.</p><div class="NLM_table-wrap" id="tbl1"><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption"><div class="NLM_caption" id=""><div class="title2">Table 1. Electrochemical Performance of Different Anodes in Sodium Half-Cells</div></div></div><div class="scrollable-table-wrap" style="display: block;"><table class="table" border="0"><colgroup><col class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="row" align="left">N-doped TiO<sub>2</sub> <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref30" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref30" aria-label="reference 30">(30)</a></td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">300</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">840</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">78.1</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">∼250</td></tr><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="row" align="left">Na<sub>2/3</sub>Co<sub>1/3</sub>Ti<sub>2/3</sub>O<sub>2</sub> <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref6" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref6" aria-label="reference 6">(6)</a></td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">3000</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">500</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">84.8</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">∼50</td></tr><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="row" align="left">Na<sub>0.66</sub>Ni<sub>0.17</sub>Co<sub>0.17</sub>Ti<sub>0.66</sub>O<sub>2</sub> <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref7" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref7" aria-label="reference 7">(7)</a></td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">300</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">20</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">88.3</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">∼100</td></tr><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="row" align="left"><b>amorphous P</b><sub><b>2</b></sub><b>S</b><sub><b>5</b></sub><b>/C (this work)</b></td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char="."><b>4000</b></td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char="."><b>2000</b></td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char="."><b>89.4</b></td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char="."><b>∼400</b></td></tr></tbody></table></div></div><p class="last">In summary, P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>/C composite is prepared using a simple long-time high energy ball-milling method and its reaction mechanism with Na is investigated. The electrode demonstrates a high reversible capacity of 396 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at 100 mA g<sup>–1</sup>, an outstanding capacity retention (99.5% after 100 cycles at 100 mA g<sup>–1</sup>), and a moderate capacity at high rate (114 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at 2 A g<sup>–1</sup>). Even when the amorphous P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>/C is cycled over 4000 times at 2 A g<sup>–1</sup>, a high capacity retention of 89.4% is achieved. The good performance may benefit from the amorphous of P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub> and the homodisperse of P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub> into carbon matrix. In the current drive to discover and optimize materials for specific energy storage, the P<sub>2</sub>S<sub>5</sub>/C composite can pave a new way for the next generation of low-cost, high-energy sodium-ion batteries.</p><div class="NLM_back"><div class="article_supporting-info" id="notes-1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i2">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge on the <a href="/" class="ext-link">ACS Publications website</a> at DOI: <a href="/doi/abs/10.1021/acsami.7b14673" class="ext-link">10.1021/acsami.7b14673</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">XRD patterns, SEM images, selected area electron-diffraction pattern, TG-DTA curves, charge–discharge curves, d<i>Q</i>/d<i>V</i> curves, and EIS curves (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b14673/suppl_file/am7b14673_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b14673/suppl_file/am7b14673_si_001.pdf">am7b14673_si_001.pdf (2.13 MB)</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="testing" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.7b14673" data-url="https://widgets.figshare.com/static/figshare.js" id="figshare-widget" style="display: block;"></div><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzone3" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzone3"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="85b54935-30e9-4058-a6d2-0b40fb754a85" class="mb-4">

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Energy prodn. and storage have become key issues concerning our welfare in daily life.  Present challenges for batteries are twofold.  In the first place, the increasing demand for powering systems of portable electronic devices and zero-emission vehicles stimulates research towards high energy and high voltage systems.  In the second place, low cost batteries are required in order to advance towards smart elec. grids that integrate discontinuous energy flow from renewable sources, optimizing the performance of clean energy sources.  Na-ion batteries can be the key for the second point, because of the huge availability of sodium, its low price and the similarity of both Li and Na insertion chemistries.  In spite of the lower energy d. and voltage of Na-ion based technologies, they can be focused on applications where the wt. and footprint requirement is less drastic, such as elec. grid storage.  Much work has to be done in the field of Na-ion in order to catch up with Li-ion technol.  Cathodic and anodic materials must be optimized, and new electrolytes will be the key point for Na-ion success.  This review will gather the up-to-date knowledge about Na-ion battery materials, with the aim of providing a wide view of the systems that have already been explored and a starting point for the new research on this battery technol.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref6" class="refNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit6" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201404549"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, H.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The electrochem. performance of mesoporous carbon (C)/tin (Sn) anodes in Na-ion and Li-ion batteries is systematically investigated.  The mesoporous C/Sn anodes in a Na-ion battery shows similar cycling stability but lower capacity and poorer rate capability than that in a Li-ion battery.  The desodiation potentials of Sn anodes are approx. 0.21 V lower than delithiation potentials.  The low capacity and poor rate capability of C/Sn anode in Na-ion batteries is mainly due to the large Na-ion size, resulting in slow Na-ion diffusion and large vol. change of porous C/Sn composite anode during alloy/dealloy reactions.  Understanding of the reaction mechanism between Sn and Na ions will provide insight towards exploring and designing new alloy-based anode materials for Na-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref10" class="refNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit10" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.6b00641"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mao, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fan, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, C.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Building Self-Healing Alloy Architecture for Stable Sodium-Ion Battery Anodes: A Case Study of Tin Anode Materials</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl.                         cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Building Self-Healing Alloy Architecture for Stable Sodium-Ion Battery Anodes: A Case Study of Tin Anode Materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Mao, Jianfeng; Fan, Xiulin; Luo, Chao; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7147-7155</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The rational design of anode materials is a challenge in developing sodium ion batteries.  Alloy anodes provide high gravimetric and volumetric capacities but suffer the short cycle life as a result of the continuous and accumulated pulverization, resulting from a large vol. change during the cycling process.  Herein, using pure Sn, an irreversible conversion reaction combined with an alloy reaction (SnO), and a reversible conversion reaction combined with an alloy reaction (Sn4P3) as samples, the pulverization and aggregation of the alloy anode can be partially recovered and the accumulation of pulverization and aggregation during charge/discharge cycles can be terminated using a reversible conversion reaction combined with an alloy reaction.  The cycling stability of three Sn-based anodes increases in order of Sn4P3 &gt; SnO &gt; Sn.  The enhancement in Sn4P3 can be attributed to a reversible reaction of Sn4P3 + 9Na ↔ 4Sn + 3Na3P, which repairs the cracks, damage, and aggregation of Sn particles that occurred in the alloy process of 4Sn + 15Na ↔ Na15Sn4 during cycling and, hence, terminates the pulverization.  The repair mechanism looks like the self-healing feature, where the damage can be healed by itself.  Therefore, the suggested mechanism can be called self-healing, while the repaired anode can be termed as the self-healing anode.  The use of self-healing strategies to build an electrode architecture is new and highly desirable because it can increase the cycle life and provide a general approach toward stable electrode materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref11" class="refNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit11" data-doi="10.1039/C3EE42944J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, X.                         cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enhanced Sodium-Ion Battery Performance by Structural Phase Transition from Two-Dimensional Hexagonal-SnS2 to Orthorhombic-SnS</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Tengfei; Pang, Wei Kong; Zhang, Chaofeng; Yang, Jianping; Chen, Zhixin; Liu, Hua Kun; Guo, Zaiping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8323-8333</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Structural phase transitions can be used to alter the properties of a material without adding any addnl. elements and are therefore of significant technol. value.  It was found that the hexagonal-SnS2 phase can be transformed into the orthorhombic-SnS phase after an annealing step in an argon atm., and the thus transformed SnS shows enhanced sodium-ion storage performance over that of the SnS2, which is attributed to its structural advantages.  Here, we provide the first report on a SnS@graphene architecture for application as a sodium-ion battery anode, which is built from two-dimensional SnS and graphene nanosheets as complementary building blocks.  The as-prepd. SnS@graphene hybrid nanostructured composite delivers an excellent specific capacity of 940 mAh/g and impressive rate capability of 492 and 308 mAh/g after 250 cycles at the current densities of 810 and 7290 mA/g, resp.  The performance was found to be much better than those of most reported anode materials for Na-ion batteries.  On the basis of combined ex situ Fourier transform IR spectroscopy, XPS, and ex situ X-ray diffraction, the formation mechanism of SnS@graphene and the synergistic Na-storage reactions of SnS in the anode are discussed in detail.  The SnS experienced a two-structural-phase transformation mechanism (orthorhombic-SnS to cubic-Sn to orthorhombic-Na3.75Sn), while the SnS2 experienced a three-structural-phase transformation mechanism (hexagonal-SnS2 to tetragonal-Sn to orthorhombic-Na3.75Sn) during the sodiation process.  The lesser structural changes of SnS during the conversion are expected to lead to good structural stability and excellent cycling stability in its sodium-ion battery performance.  These results demonstrate that the SnS@graphene architecture offers unique characteristics suitable for high-performance energy storage application.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref16" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2017.03.093"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mao, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Pang, W.                         cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Large-scale synthesis of ternary Sn5SbP3/C composite by ball milling for superior stable sodium-ion battery anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Wenchao; Mao, Jianfeng; Pang, Wei Kong; Guo, Zaiping; Chen, Zhixin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Alloy-based materials (i.e. Sn, Sb, P) are promising candidates for Na-ion battery (SIB) anodes, but they suffer from capacity decay during charge/discharge cycling due to the pulverization caused by their huge vol. change.  Nanostructures can slow down the capacity fade, but most of the synthesis methods of such nanostructured anodes are difficult to scale-up.  Herein, a ternary Sn5SbP3/C composite was fabricated by a green, low cost, 1-step and easily scalable ball-milling of elementary Sn, Sb, P, and C.  The microstructure of the ball-milled powders consists of micrometric agglomerates of active nano Sn4P3 and SnSb and Sn particles.  C in the composite acts as a conducting matrix, and it does not only benefit to the ball milling efficiency, but also benefit to the cycle life of the electrode.  Each of the active Sn4P3 and SnSb and Sn phases in the composite functions mutually as a buffer for the others.  As a result, this ternary composite anode delivers a good capacity of 352 mA h g-1 at the c.d. of 2 A g-1, which is notably higher than that of the binary Sn4P3/C and SnSb/C composites produced under the same conditions.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref17" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1039/C4CC00294F"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Y.-X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Seng, K.                 <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this work, a solvothermal strategy combined with following calcination was developed to synthesize a mesoporous NaTi2(PO4)3/CMK-3 nanohybrid as a high-performance anode for next-generation Na-ion batteries.  Physicochem. characterizations demonstrated that NASICON-type structured NaTi2(PO4)3 nanoparticles with high crystallinity were homogeneously embedded in the mesoporous CMK-3 matrix.  The mesoporous NaTi2(PO4)3/C nanohybrid as the anode for Na-ion batteries exhibited excellent electrochem. performance with high charge-discharge capability, good rate performance and long cycle life in nonaq. electrolytes.  The nanohybrid electrode delivered large specific capacities of 101, 76, 58, 39 mA-h/g at 0.2C, 0.5C, 1.0C and 2.0C, resp., and the specific capacity was still as high as 62.9 mA-h/g even after 1000 cycles at 0.5C.  Compared to the pure NaTi2(PO4)3 electrode, the mesoporous NaTi2(PO4)3/C hybrid anode with unique "meso-nano" architecture exhibited better Na-storage ability and indicated its promising application for rechargeable Na-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref27" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1039/C5TA00528K"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, D. X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, M.                 10.1039/C5TA00528K</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D3%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D8636-8642%26journal%3DJ.%2BMater.%2BChem.%2BA%26author%3DD.%2BX.%2BWang%26author%3DN.%2BChen%26author%3DM.%2BL.%2BLi%26author%3DC.%2BZ.%2BWang%26author%3DH.%2BEhrenberg%26author%3DX.%2BF.%2BBie%26author%3DY.%2BJ.%2BWei%26author%3DG.%2BChen%26author%3DF.%2BDu%26title%3DNa3V2%2528PO4%25293%252FC%2BComposite%2Bas%2BThe%2BIntercalation-Type%2BAnode%2BMaterial%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%2Bwith%2BSuperior%2BRate%2BCapability%2Band%2BLong-Cycle%2BLife%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC5TA00528K&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b14673&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC5TA00528K&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na3V2(PO4)3/C composite as the intercalation-type anode material for sodium-ion batteries with superior rate capability and long-cycle life</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Dongxue; Chen, Nan; Li, Malin; Wang, Chunzhong; Ehrenberg, Helmut; Bie, Xiaofei; Wei, Yingjin; Chen, Gang; Du, Fei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">16</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8636-8642</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A Na3V2(PO4)3/C (NVP/C) composite is successfully synthesized by sol-gel method and examd. as an anode material for sodium-ion batteries by means of galvanostatic charge-discharge profiles, cyclic voltammetry, rate performance and cyclic voltammetry comprehensively.  The NVP/C electrode delivers a reversible capacity of about 170 mA-h/g between 3.0 and 0.01 V at a c.d. of 20 mA/g corresponding to three sodium ions insertion/extn. processes.  Besides the voltage plateau at 1.57 V, another novel working platform at around 0.28 V is found for the first time in both charging and discharging profiles, possibly owing to the further redn. of vanadium.  NVP/C exhibits an excellent rate capability and long-cycle stability with a capacity retention of 62% after 3000 cycles at a high charge rate of 10C (2 A/g).  Moreover, the intercalation-type Na-ions storage mechanism is proposed on the basis of ex situ x-ray diffraction and high-resoln. transmission electron microscopy.  Our findings reveal that the NVP/C sample is a promising anode material for sodium-ion batteries due to its superior rate capability and long cycle life.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref28" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1039/C4TA06186A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ramireddy, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xing, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Rahman, M. M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dutercq, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gunzelmann, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Glushenkov, A. M.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Phosphorus-Carbon Nanocomposite Anodes for Lithium-Ion and Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Mater. Chem. A</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">3</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">5572</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">5584</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C4TA06186A</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D3%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D5572-5584%26journal%3DJ.%2BMater.%2BChem.%2BA%26author%3DT.%2BRamireddy%26author%3DT.%2BXing%26author%3DM.%2BM.%2BRahman%26author%3DY.%2BChen%26author%3DQ.%2BDutercq%26author%3DD.%2BGunzelmann%26author%3DA.%2BM.%2BGlushenkov%26title%3DPhosphorus-Carbon%2BNanocomposite%2BAnodes%2Bfor%2BLithium-Ion%2Band%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC4TA06186A&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b14673&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC4TA06186A&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Phosphorus-carbon nanocomposite anodes for lithium-ion and sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ramireddy, Thrinathreddy; Xing, Tan; Rahman, Md Mokhlesur; Chen, Ying; Dutercq, Quentin; Gunzelmann, Daniel; Glushenkov, Alexey M.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">10</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5572-5584</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">With the expected theor. capacity of 2596 mA h g-1, P is considered to be the highest capacity anode material for Na-ion batteries and one of the most attractive anode materials for Li-ion systems.  This work presents a comprehensive study of P-C nanocomposite anodes for both Li-ion and Na-ion batteries.  The composite electrodes are able to display high initial capacities of ∼1700 and 1300 mA h g-1 in Li and Na half-cells, resp., when the cells are tested within a larger potential windows of 2.0-0.01 V vs. Li/Li+ and Na/Na+.  The level of demonstrated capacity is underpinned by the storage mechanism, based on the transformation of P to Li3P phase for Li cells and an incomplete transformation to Na3P phase for Na cells.  The capacity deteriorates upon cycling, which is shown to originate from disintegration of electrodes and their delamination from current collectors by post-cycling ex situ electron microscopy.  Stable cyclic performance at the level of ∼700 and ∼350-400 mA h g-1 can be achieved if the potential windows are restricted to 2.0-0.67 V vs. Li/Li+ for Li and 2-0.33 vs. Na/Na+ for Na half-cells.  The results are critically discussed in light of literature reports.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref29" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1039/c3ta12040f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Baggetto, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Allcorn, E.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Unocic, R. M.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Mo<sub>3</sub>Sb<sub>7</sub> as A Very Fast Anode Material for Lithium-Ion and Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Mater. Chem. A</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">1</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">11163</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">11169</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/c3ta12040f</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D1%26publication_year%3D2013%26pages%3D11163-11169%26journal%3DJ.%2BMater.%2BChem.%2BA%26author%3DL.%2BBaggetto%26author%3DE.%2BAllcorn%26author%3DR.%2BR.%2BUnocic%26author%3DA.%2BManthiram%26author%3DG.%2BM.%2BVeith%26title%3DMo3Sb7%2Bas%2BA%2BVery%2BFast%2BAnode%2BMaterial%2Bfor%2BLithium-Ion%2Band%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1039%252Fc3ta12040f&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b14673&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2Fc3ta12040f&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Mo3Sb7 as a very fast anode material for lithium-ion and sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Baggetto, Loic; Allcorn, Eric; Unocic, Raymond R.; Manthiram, Arumugam; Veith, Gabriel M.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">1</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">37</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11163-11169</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Mo3Sb7 thin films prepd. by magnetron sputtering are evaluated as an anode material for Li-ion and Na-ion batteries.  The as-deposited films are amorphous and composed of small agglomerated domains with an overall Sb/Mo ratio of 2.34 that is almost identical to the ratio measured for the starting powder and the expected nominal ratio of 2.33.  When cycled with Li and Na, the films show large storage capacities of ∼430 and 330 mA h g-1, resp., with good capacity retention.  Micron thick films retain large capacities of ∼310 and 280 mA h g-1 at very high rates of 100 and 30 C-rate currents for Li and Na, resp.  The XRD study of the changes in the structure of the electrode material reveals that Li3Sb forms at full discharge whereas the electrode at full charge is amorphous.  For the reaction with Na, the electrode material remains amorphous.  Anal. of the surface chem. characterized by XPS suggests the formation of an inorg. layer (LiF, LixPOyFz) covered by org. products (carbonates, esters, ethers) in the case of Li and the formation of an org. layer only (carbonates) in the case of Na.  The electrode surface is visible at full charge for Na, thereby indicating that the Solid Electrolyte Interphase (SEI) layer is thinner when cycling with Na compared to that with Li.  Overall, the results highlight the potential of Mo3Sb7 as an anode for Li- and Na-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref30" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1039/C4TA05611F"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, Y.
